# gjsify ŌĆö Project Status

> **Current state (v0.4.14, 2026-05-19, post-Phase-G.5):** Phase G.5 lands `gjsify upgrade` ŌĆö a drop-in replacement for `yarn upgrade-interactive` / `npx npm-check-updates`. Interactive prompt by default (index ranges, `a`/`all`, comma+space separators); non-interactive bulk-update modes via `--latest` (allows major), `--minor` (skips major), `--patch` (patches only). Workspace-aware: skips `workspace:` / `file:` / `link:` / `git:` / `git+` / `http(s):` / `npm:` / `*` / `latest` specs and only checks real npm dependencies. Range prefix is preserved on write-back (`^1.2.3` ŌåÆ `^2.0.0`, `~0.4.0` ŌåÆ `~0.5.0`). Registry resolution honors layered `.npmrc` lookup (home ŌåÆ cwd) with `npm_config_registry` env var winning. Parallel fetch with 8-worker concurrency cap via `@gjsify/npm-registry`'s `fetchPackument`. Color-coded diff table (red=major / yellow=minor / green=patch / cyan=prerelease). 7-test e2e suite stands up a mock npm registry in-process via `http.createServer()` ŌĆö the test runner uses `execFile` (async) rather than `execFileSync` so the in-process mock can actually serve responses (synchronous spawn blocks the event loop and starves the HTTP server). Covers `--latest --dry-run` (no write-back), `--latest` (write with prefix preserved), `--patch` / `--minor` semver gating, `--filter` substring narrowing, `workspace:` ranges skipped, empty-deps graceful exit. Earlier (post-Phase-G.4): Phase G.4 lands `gjsify test` ŌĆö a build+run+aggregate runner that collapses the per-package `build:test:{gjs,node}` + `test:{gjs,node}` + `test` script boilerplate. Locates `src/test.mts`, builds it in-process via `BuildAction` for each requested runtime (`--runtime gjs|node|all`), runs each output (`runGjsBundle` for GJS, `spawn('node', ŌĆ”)` for Node), prints a per-runtime summary, and aggregates exit codes. mtime-based skip-when-fresh (overridable via `--rebuild`); `--no-build` runs an existing bundle. 5-test e2e suite covers happy path, failing spec, `--rebuild`, `--no-build`, missing entry. Earlier (post-Phase-F.9.7): Phase F.9.7 is the small-but-load-bearing fix surfaced by the easy6502 migration: `gjsify.flatpak.name` config field overrides the derived display name in MetaInfo `<name>` + .desktop `Name=`. Previously `flatpak init` ran the npm `package.json#name` through `friendlyName(pkgName, appId)` to pick a default ŌĆö works when name is the reverse-DNS app id, breaks when it's an npm shape like `learn6502` vs display `"Learn 6502 Assembly"`. Fix is one optional field + a 1-line `flatpak.name ?? friendlyName(...)` precedence rule in init; full backwards compatibility. Companion: easy6502 (`JumpLink/Learn6502#96`) consumes this in its migration off hand-written manifest + MetaInfo + .desktop, regenerating all four Flathub assets from a single `package.json#gjsify.flatpak` config block (including translator hints for all 12 releases). Earlier in this stretch (post-Phase-F.9.6): Phase F.9.6 extended the F.9 scaffold to cover the full AppStream surface ŌĆö `description` accepts a `DescriptionBlock[]` union (mixed `<p>` paragraphs and `<ul>/<li>` bullet lists), per-release `<description>` blocks (same shape), translator hints (`<!-- TRANSLATORS: ... -->` emitted before every translatable tag for `xgettext`/`msgfmt --xml --template` to forward into `.po` files), `<developer><email>` + `<name translate="no">`, content_rating attributes (`<content_attribute>` children), kudos, provides (binaries + mimetypes + dbus), supports/requires/recommends (controls + display_length + internet), iconRemote, translateUrl, plus screenshot captions with their own translator hints. Backwards compatible: the simple `description: "string"` form still works. The scaffold now produces MetaInfo XML rich enough to match hand-written Flathub manifests like easy6502 / Workbench, making multi-language Flathub apps generatable from a single `package.json#gjsify.flatpak` config block. Implementation: scaffold.ts rewritten from template-substitution to direct XML construction (~330 LOC builder; the old `metainfo-{app,cli}.xml.tmpl` files are removed). e2e suite extended 13 ŌåÆ 14 tests. Earlier in this stretch (post-Phase-F.9): Phase F.9 extended `gjsify flatpak init` to scaffold a full Flathub-ready asset bundle in one invocation ŌĆö manifest JSON + MetaInfo XML (`desktop-application` or `console-application`, kind-aware) + `.desktop` entry (apps only) + `flathub.json` policy stub. New `--kind <app|cli>` flag (replaces `--cli-only`, which stays as a deprecated alias); new `gjsify flatpak check` command runs Flathub linters locally (appstreamcli + flatpak-builder-lint). Earlier (post-sab-native-Phase-1): `@gjsify/worker_threads` ├Ś `@gjsify/sab-native` Phase 1 landed. `Worker.postMessage(value, [sab])` and `workerData: { sab }` now route `SharedBuffer` instances across the subprocess-Worker boundary. Parent spawns each Worker with a `SOCK_SEQPACKET` socketpair (`FdChannel.makePair()`), passes the child end as inherited fd 3 via `Gio.SubprocessLauncher.take_fd`, and per-message walks the value tree for `SharedBuffer` instances, SCM_RIGHTS-sends each fd tagged with a sequence counter, then writes a JSON line with `{__sab: tag, size: N}` placeholders. The bootstrap counts placeholders per inbound JSON message and synchronously drains exactly that many fds from fd 3 ŌĆö kernel buffering guarantees the fds are ready, since `sendmsg(SCM_RIGHTS)` always completes before `write(stdin)` in the parent ŌĆö then materialises each placeholder via `SharedBuffer.fromFd(fd, size)`. Cross-process futex (`FUTEX_WAIT` / `FUTEX_WAKE` without the `_PRIVATE` flag) lets workers signal completion on shared barrier addresses. 4 new worker_threads unit tests + 1 new integration test (4 workers ├Ś SHA-256 over 1 MiB SharedBuffer; XOR-folded digest matches the in-process reference). Total: 275/275 GJS unit + 1034/1034 GJS integration + 270/270 Node unit + 1169/1169 Node integration, all green. Earlier (2026-05-18, sab-native Phase 0): the Vala/C bridge itself ŌĆö `SharedBuffer` (`memfd_create(2)` + `mmap(MAP_SHARED)`, SEQ_CST `__atomic_*`, futex wait/notify), `FdChannel` (socketpair + SCM_RIGHTS), 18 GJS specs green including a real cross-process round-trip via `Gio.SubprocessLauncher.take_fd(fd, 3)`. Wire protocol is byte-order-explicit LE so a buffer written on x86_64 reads identically on s390x. Earlier (2026-05-18, Phase F.8): Phase F.8 added `gjsify uninstall -g <pkg>` as the symmetric inverse of `install -g`, with a 4-test e2e suite. Phase F.5 fully migrated ts-for-gir CI to the Node-free `install.mjs` bootstrap (Fedora 43 container, dnf prereqs, all four workflows; three iteration rounds caught environment quirks at the source). End-to-end users can now install AND uninstall GJS apps with the same one-line `curl ŌĆ” | gjs -m -` story, no Node or npm required. Earlier (2026-05-17, post-Phase-F-MVP): Phase F MVP landed `install.mjs` (root) + `gjsify self-update` + `gjsify generate-installer`, plus a release-workflow asset-upload step. End-users can now bootstrap `@gjsify/cli` (or any GJS-runnable npm package) with a single `curl -fsSL .../install.mjs | gjs -m -` line ŌĆö no Node or npm required on the user's machine. Three cross-cutting Soup3-stream fixes shipped alongside (Accept-Encoding: identity in npm-registry, PARTIAL_INPUT-as-EOF in utils.readBytesAsync, gjs-wrapped launcher for `.gjs.mjs` bins in install-global). The new flow is gated behind the next gjsify release (which produces the `install.mjs` + `cli.gjs.mjs` + `.sha256` GitHub-release assets); CI migration of gjsify-self + ts-for-gir lands in the follow-up PR. Earlier (2026-05-17, post-Phase-E): Phase E landed `gjsify pack` + `gjsify publish` as first-class commands, replacing the last `npm pack` + `npm publish` shellouts in the gjsify release pipeline. End-to-end verified against the live npm registry in v0.4.14; every `@gjsify/*` tarball now ships with resolved `^0.4.14` dep ranges (no leaked `workspace:^`). Three sub-bugs surfaced + fixed during the v0.4.6 ŌåÆ v0.4.14 hotfix stretch: wire-filename uses unscoped basename per npm convention, URL-encoding uses npm-package-arg's `@${scope}%2f${name}` shape with lowercase `%2f`, auth lookup honors `NPM_CONFIG_USERCONFIG` (where `actions/setup-node@v6` writes the auth-token npmrc). ts-for-gir's cross-repo migration ([gjsify/ts-for-gir#393](https://github.com/gjsify/ts-for-gir/pull/393)) bumped to `@gjsify/cli@^0.4.14` and switched `publish:app`/`publish:types` to `gjsify publish`. Earlier in this stretch (2026-05-16): `@gjsify/http2` is now feature-complete and promoted Partial ŌåÆ Full. The 5-phase plan (PRs #180ŌĆō#184) replaced Soup's HTTP/2 multiplexer for the cases libsoup can't model ŌĆö h2c cleartext server (no TLS), wire-level PUSH_PROMISE delivery, native h2c client (`http2.connect(..., { nativeDispatcher: 'force' })`), client-side `'push'` event reception from server-pushed streams, GOAWAY on `server.close()`, RST_STREAM on `stream.close(code)`, GC-pinning of `SessionBridge` instances. The native dispatcher (`Http2NativeDispatcher` + `Http2NativeClientDispatcher`) runs on `Gio.SocketService` + `Gio.SocketClient` with `Gio.PollableInputStream.create_source()` watches because `Gio.Socket.create_source()` is marked `introspectable=0` and `Gio.Socket.receive()` fails caller-allocates introspection. The Vala/C-shim layer in `@gjsify/http2-native` grew a full `nghttp2_session` driver (server + client modes) with a per-stream HEADERS accumulator keyed by `frame->push_promise.promised_stream_id` for PUSH_PROMISE frames (the parent-id keying bug was caught and fixed in Phase 2). Cross-cutting fix in `ClientHttp2Session.request()`: pseudo-headers are now reliably ordered before regular headers per RFC 7540 ┬¦8.1.2.1 (Soup tolerates mis-ordered headers since it builds the HPACK frame itself; nghttp2 rejects with PROTOCOL_ERROR + RST_STREAM ŌĆö fatal against the native dispatcher). 231 GJS tests / 51 Node tests in the http2 package, all green. The Soup-backed paths (HTTP/1.1 server, ALPN-h2 server via `createSecureServer()`, h2-over-HTTPS client via Soup.Session) stay verbatim as the default ŌĆö opt-in to native via `allowHTTP1: false` (server) or `nativeDispatcher: 'force'` (client).

> **Current state (v0.4.14, 2026-05-19, post-Phase-G.3):** Phase G.3 lands `gjsify build --watch` ŌĆö rolldown's native `watch()` API wired through the CLI, with per-build duration logging, clean SIGINT shutdown, error pass-through, and `--library --watch` rejection. Closes the "Dev loop endet bei Save" gap from the Phase-G plan: developers can now save a TS file and see the bundle update without re-running `gjsify build`. Watch is npm-rolldown-only (the GJS-native engine has no watcher); calling it under the GJS-bundled CLI surfaces a precise pointer at `node lib/index.js build ... --watch`. 2-test e2e suite asserts rebuild-on-change + SIGINT cleanliness. Earlier (post-Phase-F.9.7): Phase F.9.7 is the small-but-load-bearing fix surfaced by the easy6502 migration: `gjsify.flatpak.name` config field overrides the derived display name in MetaInfo `<name>` + .desktop `Name=`. > **Current state (v0.4.14, 2026-05-19, post-Phase-F.10.{2,3}):** Phases F.10.2 + F.10.3 land alongside F.10.1 (separate PR) to complete the Flathub publishing loop. `gjsify flatpak diff` reports version drift between the local git state and the per-app Flathub tracking-repo manifest (exit 1 + actionable hint on drift, exit 0 + `Ō£ģ in sync` on match). `gjsify flatpak release vX.Y.Z` orchestrates the full release flow end-to-end: regen assets (`flatpak init --force`) ŌåÆ lint (`flatpak check`) ŌåÆ tag + push ŌåÆ open the Flathub PR (`flatpak sync-flathub`). Ordering invariant: init + check must succeed before any tag is created. Both commands support `--dry-run` for safe planning. Earlier (post-Phase-F.9.7): Phase F.9.7 is the small-but-load-bearing fix surfaced by the easy6502 migration: `gjsify.flatpak.name` config field overrides the derived display name in MetaInfo `<name>` + .desktop `Name=`. Earlier in this stretch (2026-05-16): `@gjsify/http2` is now feature-complete and promoted Partial ŌåÆ Full. The 5-phase plan (PRs #180ŌĆō#184) replaced Soup's HTTP/2 multiplexer for the cases libsoup can't model ŌĆö h2c cleartext server (no TLS), wire-level PUSH_PROMISE delivery, native h2c client (`http2.connect(..., { nativeDispatcher: 'force' })`), client-side `'push'` event reception from server-pushed streams, GOAWAY on `server.close()`, RST_STREAM on `stream.close(code)`, GC-pinning of `SessionBridge` instances. The native dispatcher (`Http2NativeDispatcher` + `Http2NativeClientDispatcher`) runs on `Gio.SocketService` + `Gio.SocketClient` with `Gio.PollableInputStream.create_source()` watches because `Gio.Socket.create_source()` is marked `introspectable=0` and `Gio.Socket.receive()` fails caller-allocates introspection. The Vala/C-shim layer in `@gjsify/http2-native` grew a full `nghttp2_session` driver (server + client modes) with a per-stream HEADERS accumulator keyed by `frame->push_promise.promised_stream_id` for PUSH_PROMISE frames (the parent-id keying bug was caught and fixed in Phase 2). Cross-cutting fix in `ClientHttp2Session.request()`: pseudo-headers are now reliably ordered before regular headers per RFC 7540 ┬¦8.1.2.1 (Soup tolerates mis-ordered headers since it builds the HPACK frame itself; nghttp2 rejects with PROTOCOL_ERROR + RST_STREAM ŌĆö fatal against the native dispatcher). 231 GJS tests / 51 Node tests in the http2 package, all green. The Soup-backed paths (HTTP/1.1 server, ALPN-h2 server via `createSecureServer()`, h2-over-HTTPS client via Soup.Session) stay verbatim as the default ŌĆö opt-in to native via `allowHTTP1: false` (server) or `nativeDispatcher: 'force'` (client).

> **Current state (v0.4.14, 2026-05-19, post-Phase-F.10.1):** Phase F.10.1 lands `gjsify flatpak sync-flathub` ŌĆö automated end-to-end sync of the per-app `flathub/<app-id>` tracking-repo manifest. After cutting a release in the upstream repo, a single `gjsify flatpak sync-flathub` resolves the latest git tag + commit, clones the Flathub tracking-repo into `$XDG_CACHE_HOME/gjsify/flathub-sync/`, surgically edits `modules[0].sources[<i>]` to pin the new `tag` + `commit`, injects an `x-checker-data` block for the Flathub auto-update bot, branches + commits + pushes, and opens the PR via `gh`. Idempotent (already-at-version short-circuits), preserves source indent (2-space matches Flathub convention), default-branch-aware (`master` vs `main`). New `gjsify.flatpak.flathubRepo` config field overrides the default `flathub/<appId>` derivation. 4-test e2e suite stubs `git` + `gh`. Earlier (post-Phase-F.9.7): Phase F.9.7 is the small-but-load-bearing fix surfaced by the easy6502 migration: `gjsify.flatpak.name` config field overrides the derived display name in MetaInfo `<name>` + .desktop `Name=`. Previously `flatpak init` ran the npm `package.json#name` through `friendlyName(pkgName, appId)` to pick a default ŌĆö works when name is the reverse-DNS app id, breaks when it's an npm shape like `learn6502` vs display `"Learn 6502 Assembly"`. Fix is one optional field + a 1-line `flatpak.name ?? friendlyName(...)` precedence rule in init; full backwards compatibility. Companion: easy6502 (`JumpLink/Learn6502#96`) consumes this in its migration off hand-written manifest + MetaInfo + .desktop, regenerating all four Flathub assets from a single `package.json#gjsify.flatpak` config block (including translator hints for all 12 releases). Earlier in this stretch (post-Phase-F.9.6): Phase F.9.6 extended the F.9 scaffold to cover the full AppStream surface ŌĆö `description` accepts a `DescriptionBlock[]` union (mixed `<p>` paragraphs and `<ul>/<li>` bullet lists), per-release `<description>` blocks (same shape), translator hints (`<!-- TRANSLATORS: ... -->` emitted before every translatable tag for `xgettext`/`msgfmt --xml --template` to forward into `.po` files), `<developer><email>` + `<name translate="no">`, content_rating attributes (`<content_attribute>` children), kudos, provides (binaries + mimetypes + dbus), supports/requires/recommends (controls + display_length + internet), iconRemote, translateUrl, plus screenshot captions with their own translator hints. Backwards compatible: the simple `description: "string"` form still works. The scaffold now produces MetaInfo XML rich enough to match hand-written Flathub manifests like easy6502 / Workbench, making multi-language Flathub apps generatable from a single `package.json#gjsify.flatpak` config block. Implementation: scaffold.ts rewritten from template-substitution to direct XML construction (~330 LOC builder; the old `metainfo-{app,cli}.xml.tmpl` files are removed). e2e suite extended 13 ŌåÆ 14 tests. Earlier in this stretch (post-Phase-F.9): Phase F.9 extended `gjsify flatpak init` to scaffold a full Flathub-ready asset bundle in one invocation ŌĆö manifest JSON + MetaInfo XML (`desktop-application` or `console-application`, kind-aware) + `.desktop` entry (apps only) + `flathub.json` policy stub. New `--kind <app|cli>` flag (replaces `--cli-only`, which stays as a deprecated alias); new `gjsify flatpak check` command runs Flathub linters locally (appstreamcli + flatpak-builder-lint). Earlier (post-sab-native-Phase-1): `@gjsify/worker_threads` ├Ś `@gjsify/sab-native` Phase 1 landed. `Worker.postMessage(value, [sab])` and `workerData: { sab }` now route `SharedBuffer` instances across the subprocess-Worker boundary. Parent spawns each Worker with a `SOCK_SEQPACKET` socketpair (`FdChannel.makePair()`), passes the child end as inherited fd 3 via `Gio.SubprocessLauncher.take_fd`, and per-message walks the value tree for `SharedBuffer` instances, SCM_RIGHTS-sends each fd tagged with a sequence counter, then writes a JSON line with `{__sab: tag, size: N}` placeholders. The bootstrap counts placeholders per inbound JSON message and synchronously drains exactly that many fds from fd 3 ŌĆö kernel buffering guarantees the fds are ready, since `sendmsg(SCM_RIGHTS)` always completes before `write(stdin)` in the parent ŌĆö then materialises each placeholder via `SharedBuffer.fromFd(fd, size)`. Cross-process futex (`FUTEX_WAIT` / `FUTEX_WAKE` without the `_PRIVATE` flag) lets workers signal completion on shared barrier addresses. 4 new worker_threads unit tests + 1 new integration test (4 workers ├Ś SHA-256 over 1 MiB SharedBuffer; XOR-folded digest matches the in-process reference). Total: 275/275 GJS unit + 1034/1034 GJS integration + 270/270 Node unit + 1169/1169 Node integration, all green. Earlier (2026-05-18, sab-native Phase 0): the Vala/C bridge itself ŌĆö `SharedBuffer` (`memfd_create(2)` + `mmap(MAP_SHARED)`, SEQ_CST `__atomic_*`, futex wait/notify), `FdChannel` (socketpair + SCM_RIGHTS), 18 GJS specs green including a real cross-process round-trip via `Gio.SubprocessLauncher.take_fd(fd, 3)`. Wire protocol is byte-order-explicit LE so a buffer written on x86_64 reads identically on s390x. Earlier (2026-05-18, Phase F.8): Phase F.8 added `gjsify uninstall -g <pkg>` as the symmetric inverse of `install -g`, with a 4-test e2e suite. Phase F.5 fully migrated ts-for-gir CI to the Node-free `install.mjs` bootstrap (Fedora 43 container, dnf prereqs, all four workflows; three iteration rounds caught environment quirks at the source). End-to-end users can now install AND uninstall GJS apps with the same one-line `curl ŌĆ” | gjs -m -` story, no Node or npm required. Earlier (2026-05-17, post-Phase-F-MVP): Phase F MVP landed `install.mjs` (root) + `gjsify self-update` + `gjsify generate-installer`, plus a release-workflow asset-upload step. End-users can now bootstrap `@gjsify/cli` (or any GJS-runnable npm package) with a single `curl -fsSL .../install.mjs | gjs -m -` line ŌĆö no Node or npm required on the user's machine. Three cross-cutting Soup3-stream fixes shipped alongside (Accept-Encoding: identity in npm-registry, PARTIAL_INPUT-as-EOF in utils.readBytesAsync, gjs-wrapped launcher for `.gjs.mjs` bins in install-global). The new flow is gated behind the next gjsify release (which produces the `install.mjs` + `cli.gjs.mjs` + `.sha256` GitHub-release assets); CI migration of gjsify-self + ts-for-gir lands in the follow-up PR. Earlier (2026-05-17, post-Phase-E): Phase E landed `gjsify pack` + `gjsify publish` as first-class commands, replacing the last `npm pack` + `npm publish` shellouts in the gjsify release pipeline. End-to-end verified against the live npm registry in v0.4.14; every `@gjsify/*` tarball now ships with resolved `^0.4.14` dep ranges (no leaked `workspace:^`). > **Previous (v0.4.0-pre, 2026-05-12, post-Phase A):** Phase A landed `output.keepNames` as the top-level minify-keepNames path so the GJS-CLI bundle now shrinks within ~12% of the Node-CLI's output for the yargs integration fixture (down from 19% delta). The previous nested `minify: { mangle: { keepNames: {...} } }` shape worked under npm rolldown's TS API but tripped `rolldown_common::deserialize_minify` on the native facade's JSON path. New 5th self-host e2e test enforces size-equivalence within 15% + semantic equivalence (both bundles produce 52 yargs tests passing). Earlier in this stretch: **Phase D-3 self-host loop closed.** `gjsify build packages/infra/cli/src/index.ts --app gjs` produces a 6.3 MB GJS bundle that runs under stock `gjs 1.88` and bundles real npm projects end-to-end ŌĆö the yargs integration suite (52 tests) builds + runs to green under `gjs -m` only, no Node anywhere in the loop. Five concrete blockers fixed across the bundler-pick + auto-globals + plugin-gjsify packages: `parseAsync()` for top-level yargs, lazy-load of npm rolldown (Rust crate can't load under GJS), engine-aware `AnalysisBundler` injection for the `--globals auto` iterative pass, `createRequire(import.meta.url).resolve(...) ŌåÆ pathToFileURL(...)` for native facade loading under GJS, six JS-API Ōåö Rust-deserializer shape normalizations (`input` ŌåÆ InputItem[], `output: {}` flattened, `transform.{define,inject}` lifted, inject map ŌåÆ tagged-enum array, `sourcemap: false` dropped, `minify: { mangle: ... }` ŌåÆ plain `true`). Plus: input-side shebang strip plugin so the CLI's own `#!/usr/bin/env node` doesn't land mid-chunk; `unicorn-magic` ESM shim mirroring the upstream Node entry; `resolveConsoleShim()` walks `node_modules` from `_shimDir`. Permanent regression coverage in `tests/e2e/self-host/` (4 tests, ~17 s) wired into the `test:e2e` aggregator. Earlier in this v0.4.0-pre stretch: Workstream B (`@gjsify/tls`) promoted from Partial ŌåÆ near-Full: cert-chain extraction (Node-shaped `getPeerCertificate({detailed:true})` walking `Gio.TlsCertificate.get_issuer()`), full RFC 6125 ┬¦6.4.3 hostname matching (wildcard prefix/suffix, xn-- A-label exact match, *.tld rejection, error code `ERR_TLS_CERT_ALTNAME_INVALID`), mTLS via `Gio.TlsConnection.set_certificate()` on both client + server, `TlsAuthenticationMode.REQUESTED/REQUIRED` for `requestCert`+`rejectUnauthorized`, custom-CA validation via `cert.verify()` against parsed `caCertificates`, custom `checkServerIdentity` override, ALPN advertise/negotiate via `set_advertised_protocols`/`get_negotiated_protocol`, `addContext`+`SNICallback` plumbing (best-effort ŌĆö Gio doesn't surface ClientHello server_name pre-handshake; tracked in Open TODOs), `createSecureContext` accepts string/Buffer/Uint8Array/array PEM with cert+key concatenation and CA-bundle splitting via `splitPemBlocks`, ctx.context Node-compat self-reference. New specs `cert.spec.ts` + `tls.gjs.spec.ts` (RFC 6125 depth/prefix/IDN, error.code, GJS-only Gio.TlsCertificate plumbing). Tests: 132 ŌåÆ 169 (+37). 65 `as any` removed from `tls/src/index.spec.ts` (all replaced by `unknown` + type guards / `fakeCert(...)` helper). Workstream C (`@gjsify/worker_threads`) added `transferList` support to `MessagePort.postMessage()` for both `ArrayBuffer` (zero-copy via SM140 `ArrayBuffer.prototype.transfer()` ŌĆö sender detaches) and `MessagePort` (in-process channel hand-off ŌĆö source port detaches, receiver gets a usable port wired to the surviving channel partner). `SharedArrayBuffer` pass-through verified on Node (same backing store; cross-thread `Atomics.{store,load,notify}` visibility) and gracefully skipped on GJS ŌĆö Mozilla disables the SAB constructor in stock GJS, and the cross-process subprocess-Worker path needs a `@gjsify/sab-native` Vala mmap bridge that's deferred to STATUS.md "Open TODOs ŌåÆ SharedArrayBuffer cross-process sharing". Implementation: `packages/gjs/utils/src/structured-clone.ts` extended with a transfer context + view-snapshot pre-walk (TypedArray/DataView byteOffset/length captured BEFORE buffer transfer detaches the source views); `packages/node/worker_threads/src/message-port.ts` rewritten to validate the transfer list (rejects detached, duplicate, non-transferable, SAB-in-list, self-transfer, closed-port-transfer with `DataCloneError`/code 25 per HTML spec), substitute MessagePort placeholders before clone, and re-attach receiver-side ports after. New integration suite `tests/integration/worker-stress/` with two specs: `transferlist-stress` (bulk 16 MiB transfer + 4-channel fan-out + 5-hop port chain ŌĆö Node 727 MiB/s, GJS 235 MiB/s baseline) and `sab-parallel-hash` (4 worker threads computing SHA-256 over a 1 MiB SAB, Atomics barrier, Node-only). 32 new unit tests + 5 integration tests in worker_threads itself; full counts now 270 Node / 264 GJS unit + 1169 Node / 1033 GJS integration. `as any` removed from `worker_threads/src/index.spec.ts` (30 ŌåÆ 0 ŌĆö added `BroadcastChannelW3C` / `MessagePortW3C` helper aliases for the W3C surface that `@types/node` types more tightly than the runtime). Earlier in this v0.4.0-pre stretch: Workstream D (`@gjsify/webgl` source refactor) split the 4164-line `webgl-context-base.ts` into focused composition modules under `packages/framework/webgl/src/ts/context/` (`state.ts`, `buffer-binding.ts`, `texture-management.ts`, `framebuffer.ts`, `shader-program.ts`, `drawing.ts`). Each module declares a typed `*Methods` interface (declaration-merged into `WebGLContextBase`) plus an `install*Methods(proto)` registration function called from the base file after the class declaration ŌĆö sidesteps the circular-import trap that prototype-merge mixins would otherwise hit at module-load time. The base file is now Ōēł590 lines, owning fields, abstract `_gl`, the constructor, `_init`, `getParameter`, `getExtension`, `getSupportedExtensions`, and the foundational `_check{Owns,Valid,Wrapper}` helpers shared by every split module. Public API unchanged ŌĆö `WebGLRenderingContext` and `WebGL2RenderingContext` (and every external consumer) work without modification. `as any` reduced from 74 to 44 across `packages/framework/webgl/src/`; webgl-context-base.ts went 2 ŌåÆ 0, webgl2-rendering-context.ts went 29 ŌåÆ 1 (a doc comment), with the remaining 44 split between intentional negative-test casts in conformance/spec files and globalThis bootstrap in `webgl-bridge.ts`. Six bare `// TODO`/`// FIXME` comments in the original file replaced by structured `STATUS.md "Open TODOs": ŌĆ”` comments alongside the now-tracked entries (drawingBufferColorSpace colorimetry, multi-FBO texture detach, MAX_RENDERBUFFER_SIZE caching, optional drawing-buffer pre-allocation). All 860 GJS WebGL tests pass, the Three.js post-processing showcase rebuilds clean. Earlier: two post-v0.3.17 `gjsify showcase` hotfixes. (a) Pre-flight `checkGwebgl` removed ŌĆö it tried to `require.resolve('@gjsify/webgl')` from `process.cwd()` or the CLI's own `node_modules`, both empty under `npx @gjsify/cli showcase three-postprocessing-pixel`, so it always failed for webgl-using showcases. Since `showcase` delegates to `gjsify dlx`, which fetches the showcase + transitive deps (incl. `@gjsify/webgl` with the `gwebgl` Vala prebuild) into the npm cache where the PR #94 native-package walker picks it up, the pre-flight was checking something `dlx` was about to install ŌĆö leftover from when the CLI tarball bundled showcase packages. (b) `gjsify showcase <name>` now pins the spawned dlx spec to the CLI's own version (`<pkg>@<cli-version>`). Without the pin, `gjsify dlx` cached whatever version it first resolved and served it for 7 days (default TTL), so users running `npx @gjsify/cli@0.3.17 showcase express-webserver` got the cached `@gjsify/example-node-express-webserver@0.3.16` install ŌĆö pre-PR #94 shape, missing the `@gjsify/http-soup-bridge` runtime dep ŌĆö and the bundle errored with `Typelib file for namespace 'GjsifyHttpSoupBridge' not found`. Pinning makes the cache key change every release, so each CLI version always runs its matching showcase tarball. Two new regression tests in `tests/e2e/cli-only/run.mjs` lock the showcase-command shape, plus a new `tests/e2e/dlx-version-pin/` suite (4 tests) that drives `gjsify dlx` end-to-end against an in-process mock npm registry ŌĆö verifies that `<pkg>@v0.0.1` and `<pkg>@v0.0.2` land in different cache directories, transitive native-typelib deps install correctly, and `computeNativeEnvForBundle` walks them. Together these would have caught the regression that necessitated the v0.3.18/0.4.14 hotfix releases without needing to publish to npm to test. Below: three coupled changes landed in one PR. (1) `gjsify dlx` / `gjsify run` native-prebuild detection now walks the bundle's own `node_modules` tree on top of CWD ŌĆö fixes `gjsify showcase express-webserver` failing with `Typelib file for namespace 'GjsifyHttpSoupBridge' not found` because transitive Vala typelibs (`@gjsify/http-soup-bridge`) were never reached. The two overlapping detectors (`detectNativePackages` + transitive-blind `resolveNativePackages`) collapse into one algorithm with two startpoints; env composition is split into the testable pure helper `computeNativeEnvForBundle(bundlePath, cwd)`. (2) Showcase shape: `@gjsify/example-node-express-webserver` now declares `@gjsify/http-soup-bridge` as a runtime `dependency` (was missing ŌĆö only present at build time, so `npm install` from the published tarball never shipped the typelib). (3) `gjsify build` minifies by default; opt-out via `--no-minify` or `bundler.output.minify: false`. The hard-coded `minify: false` overrides in the app/library orchestrators are removed so user-config now wins. New e2e suite `dlx-native-prebuilds/` (2 tests). Earlier in this v0.4.0-pre stretch: `cssAsStringPlugin` lightningcss bundling/lowering + `css-bundling` e2e suite.
>
> **Previous (v0.4.0-pre, 2026-05-07):** PR2 of the Flatpak-toolchain line landed `gjsify flatpak {init,build,deps,ci}` subcommands ŌĆö manifest scaffold from `gjsify.flatpak` config, flatpak-builder + flatpak-node-generator wrappers, GitHub-Actions workflow scaffold. New e2e suite `flatpak/` with 7 tests via stubbed binaries. PR1 had landed the bundler-side primitives (`gjsify gsettings` subcommand, `defineFromPackageJson` / `defineFromEnv` config keys, `loaders` text-shorthand, package-name plugin entries in `bundler.plugins`, env-template shebang strings) gated behind 5 new e2e suites. Consumers ŌĆö `easy6502/packages/app-gnome` (ViteŌåÆ`gjsify build` migration) and `@ts-for-gir/cli` (drop `scripts/build-gjs.mjs` wrapper) ŌĆö follow next. Earlier: the gjsify build pipeline produces a single self-contained GJS bundle from arbitrary npm-published packages. **The bundler engine has been migrated from esbuild to Rolldown** (Vite 8's production bundler) ŌĆö same CLI surface (`gjsify build --app gjs|node|browser --globals auto ŌĆ”`), Rollup-shaped plugins under the hood that also run under Vite for the sister GJS apps. `@gjsify/rolldown-plugin-gjsify` rewrites `import.meta.url` / `__dirname` / `__filename` for both regular `node_modules` and Yarn-PnP zip-resident files, and inlines statically-resolvable `readFileSync(new URL(<lit>, import.meta.url), "utf8")` / `readdirSync(URL)` / `existsSync(URL)` / `JSON.parse(readFileSync(...))` compositions at build time. `--globals auto` retains its iterative multi-pass "after tree-shaking" detection (bundler-agnostic; engine swap preserves the load-bearing invariant). `@gjsify/module`'s `createRequire` is PnP-aware ŌĆö `require.resolve("<pkg>/package.json")` works in PnP-built bundles. `@gjsify/cli` ships a native install backend (`@gjsify/semver` + `@gjsify/npm-registry` + `@gjsify/tar`) so `gjsify dlx` and `gjsify install` no longer require Node or npm at runtime. First real-world consumer: ts-for-gir's GJS bundle ([gjsify/ts-for-gir#378](https://github.com/gjsify/ts-for-gir/pull/378)) runs unmodified npm packages (TypeScript compiler, TypeDoc, shiki, yargs, ejs, ~100 transitive zip-resident deps) on `gjs -m` with zero ts-for-gir-side workarounds. End-to-end coverage: 9 e2e suites green (`create-app`, `cli-only`, `cli-only-pnp`, `standalone-plugin`, `native-install`, `cli-config`, `inline-static-reads`, `library-multi-build`, `terminal-native`). Pillar tests: Node 291/291, GJS 227/227 (3 ignored). The full v0.3.x history lives in [Release timeline](#release-timeline) below; per-release detail in [`CHANGELOG.md`](./CHANGELOG.md).

## Release timeline

- **v0.4.14** ŌĆö `@gjsify/module` PnP-aware `createRequire`. Parses `.pnp.cjs`'s `RAW_RUNTIME_STATE` directly (no Yarn-manifest execution), so `require.resolve("<pkg>/package.json")` works in PnP-built bundles for the first time. Removed the last reason ts-for-gir had to embed its EJS templates at build time.
- **v0.3.12** ŌĆö `cli,esbuild-plugin-gjsify` library multi-build fix: `format`/`jsExtension` were being passed the wrong sibling outdir/extension, so the ESM and CJS halves of a `--library` build collided in the CJS directory. New e2e suite: `library-multi-build/`.
- **v0.3.11** ŌĆö Three rewriter fixes that let PnP-built bundles run portably without `nodeLinker: node-modules`: (1) banner-shebang hoist keeps `#!/usr/bin/env -S gjs -m` at byte 0 even when esbuild's own banner runs first; (2) `createRequire(<URL>)` of zip-resident anchors becomes a thrown-on-use stub (esbuild has already inlined every dep ŌĆö the createRequire result is dead code in our bundles); (3) `import.meta.url` URL rewrite is skipped for source files inside Yarn-PnP virtual zips so the bare token resolves to the bundle's own URL at runtime.
- **v0.3.10** ŌĆö Static-read inliner: build-time evaluation of `readFileSync` / `readdirSync` / `existsSync` / `JSON.parse(readFileSync(...))` against `import.meta.url`-relative URLs, replaces calls with literal contents ŌåÆ bundle is portable to any directory. New e2e suite: `inline-static-reads/` (1/1).
- **v0.3.9** ŌĆö Config precedence + outfile safety + PnP-zip rewriter warning. `package.json#gjsify` now merges with `.gjsifyrc.*`/`gjsify.config.*` (was first-match-wins). `gjsify build` refuses to default `--outfile` to a `.ts` source path. New e2e suite: `cli-config/` (2/2).
- **v0.3.8** ŌĆö Native install backend default. `@gjsify/semver` (77/77), `@gjsify/npm-registry` (33/33), `@gjsify/tar` (27/25 Node/GJS) compose into `install-backend-native.ts` ŌĆö BFS resolver, parallel tarball download with sha512 SRI, flat `node_modules/` + `.bin/` symlinks. New e2e suite: `native-install/`.
- **v0.3.7** ŌĆö PnP-rewriter onLoad ordering fix: the `__filename`/`__dirname` rewriter is composed INTO the pnp plugin's onLoad (esbuild stops at the first match). Extracted `getPnpPlugin` from `@gjsify/cli` into reusable `@gjsify/resolve-npm/pnp-relay` with a `transformContentsFactory` callback. New e2e suite: `cli-only-pnp/` (5/5).
- **v0.3.6** ŌĆö pnpapi namespace unwrap, esbuild peer dep, lazy-deepkit. `cli-only-pnp` suite (4/4).
- **v0.3.5** ŌĆö `gjsify dlx` GJS-bundle runner; PnP zip read; two-hop relay shape; shebang config; `@gjsify/webassembly` Promise-API polyfill (15 tests).
- **v0.3.0ŌĆō0.3.4** ŌĆö Yarn PnP support, `excludeGlobals`, fetch bridge-free, UNDECLARED_DEPENDENCY fall-through, portable `import.meta.url`.

## Summary

gjsify implements Node.js, Web Standard, and DOM APIs for GJS (GNOME JavaScript / SpiderMonkey 140).
The project comprises **44 Node.js packages** (+1 meta), **20 Web API packages** (+1 meta), **8 DOM/bridge packages**, **4 GJS infrastructure packages**, and **9 build/infra tools**.

| Category | Total | Full | Partial | Stub |
|----------|-------|------|---------|------|
| Node.js APIs | 43 | 36 (84%) | 4 (9%) | 4 (9%) |
| Node.js meta | 1 | 1 | ŌĆö | ŌĆö |
| Web APIs | 20 | 18 (90%) | 2 (10%) | ŌĆö |
| Web meta | 1 | 1 | ŌĆö | ŌĆö |
| DOM / Bridges | 8 | 8 (100%) | ŌĆö | ŌĆö |
| Browser UI | 3 | 3 (adwaita-web, adwaita-fonts, adwaita-icons) | ŌĆö | ŌĆö |
| Showcases | 8 | 8 | ŌĆö | ŌĆö |
| GJS Infrastructure | 4 | 3 | 1 (types) | ŌĆö |
| Build/Infra Tools | 9 | 9 | ŌĆö | ŌĆö |
| Integration test suites | 4 | 4 (webtorrent, socket.io, streamx, autobahn) | ŌĆö | ŌĆö |

**Test coverage:** 10,570+ test cases in 112+ spec files (each test runs on both Node.js and GJS). CI via GitHub Actions (Node.js 24.x + GJS on Fedora 43/44 ŌĆö minimum supported runtime: GJS 1.86 / SpiderMonkey 140). Integration suites (`yarn test:integration`) are opt-in and exercise curated upstream tests from webtorrent / socket.io / streamx, plus the Autobahn fuzzingserver for RFC 6455 compliance.

| **util** | ŌĆö | 245 (2 specs) | inspect (**colors, styles, custom symbol, defaultOptions**, edge cases), format (%%, %s/%d/%j/%i/%f, args), promisify (**custom symbol**), callbackify, deprecate, inherits (**super_**), isDeepStrictEqual, **types** (isDate/RegExp/Map/Set/Promise/ArrayBuffer/TypedArray/Async/Generator/WeakMap/WeakSet/DataView), TextEncoder/TextDecoder |
| **zlib** | ŌĆö | 102 | gzip/deflate/deflateRaw round-trip, constants, Unicode, binary, cross-format errors, sync methods, double compression, consistency |

### Native Bridges

| Package | GNOME Libs | Description |
|---------|-----------|-------------|
| **@gjsify/terminal-native** (Vala) | Linux/Posix (Vala VAPIs) | Optional Vala prebuild providing real Linux terminal syscalls to `@gjsify/tty` and `@gjsify/process`. `Terminal` class: `is_tty(fd)` ŌåÆ `Posix.isatty()`, `get_size(fd, out rows, out cols, out xpixel, out ypixel)` ŌåÆ `ioctl(TIOCGWINSZ)`, `set_raw_mode(fd, enable)` ŌåÆ `tcgetattr/tcsetattr` (ICANON+ECHO). `ResizeWatcher` class: `resized(rows, cols)` GObject signal wired to SIGWINCH via `GLib.Unix.signal_add()`. TypeScript wrapper: synchronous `imports.gi.GjsifyTerminal` with try/catch ŌĆö safe when typelib not installed, no crash. Consumers see native behaviour when installed, GLib/env fallback otherwise. Ships as `.so`+`.typelib` in `prebuilds/linux-x86_64/`. CI builds pending (add to `.github/workflows/prebuilds.yml`). |
| **@gjsify/http-soup-bridge** (Vala) | Soup 3.0 | Vala/GObject library consumed by `@gjsify/http`. Wraps `Soup.Server` + `SoupServerMessage` and exposes JS only through plain GObject classes whose lifetime SpiderMonkey GC cannot race against. Solves two libsoup GC crashes: (1) `BoxedBase::finalize ŌåÆ g_source_unref` SIGSEGV from deferred-GC on in-flight Soup messages, (2) `g_main_context_unref` assertion from shared `GMainContext` ref imbalance. Contains `Server` (wraps `Soup.Server`, emits `request-received` / `upgrade` / `error-occurred` signals), `Request` (read-side snapshot ŌĆö method, url, headers, `get_body()`), `Response` (write side, owns `SoupServerMessage` C-side including all pause/unpause bookkeeping), and a peer-close watcher (`g_socket_create_source(IN|HUP|ERR)` + non-blocking `MSG_PEEK` probe ŌĆö capability unreachable from JS because `Gio.Socket.receive_message` is not introspectable). Ships as prebuilt `.so` + `.typelib` in `prebuilds/linux-{x86_64,aarch64,ppc64,s390x,riscv64}/`; CI (`.github/workflows/prebuilds.yml`) rebuilds on Vala source changes (native runners for x86_64/aarch64; QEMU via `uraimo/run-on-arch-action` for ppc64/s390x/riscv64). |
| **@gjsify/http2-native** (Vala + C shim) | libnghttp2 Ōēź 1.40 | Vala/GObject library consumed by `@gjsify/http2`. Provides nghttp2 primitives unreachable through libsoup's high-level GIR API. Contains `FrameEncoder` (HPACK header-block encoder + raw frame builders for DATA / HEADERS / PUSH_PROMISE / SETTINGS / WINDOW_UPDATE / PING / RST_STREAM / GOAWAY ŌĆö backed by a tiny C shim around `nghttp2_hd_deflate_*` since nghttp2 has no upstream Vala VAPI), `StreamIdAllocator` (server-side even-id sequencer per RFC 7540 ┬¦5.1.1, plus client-id tracking for GOAWAY), and **`SessionBridge`** (full `nghttp2_session` driver ŌĆö server + client modes via `nghttp2_session_{server,client}_new`, `mem_recv`/`mem_send`, complete submit family (`submit_settings/response/request/data/push_promise/goaway/rst_stream`); per-stream HEADERS accumulator + GLib.Bytes-owned DATA carrier; events drain through `gjsify_http2_event_*` getters and re-emit on the main loop via `GLib.Idle.add()` ŌĆö same hop pattern as `@gjsify/webrtc-native`). Header signals carry `GLib.Variant("a(ss)")` instead of `string[]` so GJS's marshaller doesn't trip the `G_VALUE_HOLDS_POINTER` assertion. All buffer ownership stays C-side via `GLib.Bytes` so SpiderMonkey GC cannot race nghttp2 allocations ŌĆö same pattern as `@gjsify/webrtc-native` / `@gjsify/http-soup-bridge`. TS wrapper loads the typelib lazily via try/catch ŌĆö packages fall back to JS-only counters when the prebuild is unavailable. Ships as `.so` + `.typelib` in `prebuilds/linux-{x86_64,aarch64,ppc64,s390x,riscv64}/`; CI (`.github/workflows/prebuilds.yml`) rebuilds on Vala source changes. |
| **@gjsify/sab-native** (Vala + C shim) | Linux libc (memfd_create, mmap, futex, socketpair, SCM_RIGHTS) | Vala/GObject library providing cross-process shared memory + atomics for `@gjsify/worker_threads`. Closes the SharedArrayBuffer gap in stock GJS (Mozilla disables the SAB constructor without COOP/COEP opts; even with SAB on, subprocess workers cannot share backing stores by design ŌĆö SM allocates SABs from the per-runtime malloc heap). Two GObject classes: **`SharedBuffer`** (wraps a `memfd_create(2)` + `mmap(MAP_SHARED)` region, exposes typed accessors `get_u8/u32_le/i32_le/u64_le` + write counterparts, bulk `read_bytes/write_bytes` via `GLib.Bytes` with refcount-pinned mmap lifetime, SEQ_CST atomics `atomic_{add,sub,load,store,xchg,cmpxchg}_i32` via GCC `__atomic_*` builtins, and `futex_wait/futex_wake` via raw `syscall(SYS_futex, FUTEX_{WAIT,WAKE}_PRIVATE)` for cross-process wait/notify) + **`FdChannel`** (Unix-domain `SOCK_SEQPACKET` socketpair + `sendmsg/recvmsg` with `SCM_RIGHTS` for fd-transfer; SOCK_CLOEXEC on both ends; 4-byte big-endian tag payload mapping each fd to the JSON-side placeholder index). Two construction paths: `SharedBuffer.create(size)` allocates fresh anonymous memory; `SharedBuffer.from_fd(fd, size)` mmaps a fd received over `SCM_RIGHTS`. Fd dup'd on `from_fd` so sender can close their copy. Wire protocol is byte-order-explicit LE across all multi-byte accessors so a buffer written on x86_64 reads identically on s390x. TS fa├¦ade (`SharedBuffer`, `atomics` namespace, internal `fdChannel`) loads typelib via synchronous `imports.gi.GjsifySabNative` with try/catch ŌĆö `hasNativeSab()` predicate. 18 GJS specs green including a real `Gio.SubprocessLauncher.take_fd(fd, 3)` cross-process round-trip + SCM_RIGHTS fd transfer round-trip. Ships as `.so` + `.gir` + `.typelib` in `prebuilds/linux-{x86_64,aarch64,ppc64,s390x,riscv64}/`. |

### WebRTC Status

**Implemented (Phase 1 + 1.5 ŌĆö Data Channel end-to-end):**
- RTCPeerConnection: constructor, createOffer, createAnswer, setLocalDescription, setRemoteDescription, addIceCandidate, close, createDataChannel, getConfiguration
- State getters: signalingState, connectionState, iceConnectionState, iceGatheringState, localDescription, remoteDescription, currentLocal/RemoteDescription, pendingLocal/RemoteDescription, canTrickleIceCandidates
- RTCPeerConnection events: negotiationneeded, icecandidate, icegatheringstatechange, iceconnectionstatechange, connectionstatechange, signalingstatechange, datachannel
- RTCDataChannel: send (string / ArrayBuffer / ArrayBufferView / Blob), close, readyState, bufferedAmount, bufferedAmountLowThreshold, binaryType ('arraybuffer' default, 'blob' lazy via globalThis.Blob), id, label, ordered, protocol, negotiated, maxPacketLifeTime, maxRetransmits
- RTCDataChannel events: open, close, message, error, bufferedamountlow, closing
- RTCSessionDescription (with GstŌåöJS round-trip via GstSDP), RTCIceCandidate (W3C fields + candidate-line parser), RTCError (extends DOMException), RTCErrorEvent, RTCPeerConnectionIceEvent, RTCDataChannelEvent

**Implemented (Phase 2 ŌĆö Media API Surface):**
- RTCPeerConnection.addTransceiver(kind, init) ŌĆö creates real GstWebRTC transceivers, returns RTCRtpTransceiver
- RTCPeerConnection.getSenders / getReceivers / getTransceivers ŌĆö return live lists
- RTCPeerConnection.removeTrack(sender) ŌĆö validates sender, resets track
- RTCPeerConnection `track` event ŌĆö fires on pad-added with RTCTrackEvent (receiver, track, streams, transceiver)
- RTCRtpTransceiver: mid, direction (read/write, mapped to GstWebRTC enum), currentDirection, stop(), setCodecPreferences(codecs)
- RTCRtpSender: track, dtmf, transport, getParameters/setParameters, replaceTrack (stub), getCapabilities(kind)
- RTCRtpReceiver: track (stub MediaStreamTrack, muted), jitterBufferTarget (0ŌĆō4000ms range), getParameters, getCapabilities(kind)
- MediaStream: id, active, getTracks/getAudioTracks/getVideoTracks, getTrackById, addTrack/removeTrack, clone, addtrack/removetrack events
- MediaStreamTrack: id, kind, label, enabled, muted, readyState, contentHint, clone, stop
- MediaStreamTrackEvent, RTCTrackEvent
- Globals via `@gjsify/webrtc/register/media`: MediaStream, MediaStreamTrack, RTCTrackEvent

**Implemented (Phase 2.5 ŌĆö Incoming Media Pipeline):**
- ReceiverBridge (Vala): manages muted source ŌåÆ decodebin ŌåÆ tee switching entirely in C to handle decodebin's streaming-thread `pad-added` signal
- RTCRtpReceiver._connectToPad wires webrtcbin output ŌåÆ ReceiverBridge ŌåÆ media-flowing signal ŌåÆ track unmute
- Track transitions from muted to unmuted when decoded media replaces the muted source
- Pipeline cleanup on RTCPeerConnection.close() disposes receiver bridges

**Implemented (Phase 3 ŌĆö Outgoing Media + getUserMedia):**
- RTCPeerConnection.addTrack(track, ...streams) ŌĆö creates transceiver, wires outgoing pipeline via request_pad_simple
- getUserMedia({ audio, video }) ŌĆö wraps GStreamer sources (pipewiresrc ŌåÆ pulsesrc ŌåÆ autoaudiosrc ŌåÆ audiotestsrc fallback; pipewiresrc ŌåÆ v4l2src ŌåÆ autovideosrc ŌåÆ videotestsrc fallback)
- MediaDevices class with getUserMedia, enumerateDevices (stub), getSupportedConstraints
- navigator.mediaDevices registration via `@gjsify/webrtc/register/media-devices`
- Outgoing pipeline: source ŌåÆ valve ŌåÆ audioconvert/videoconvert ŌåÆ encoder (opusenc/vp8enc) ŌåÆ payloader (rtpopuspay/rtpvp8pay) ŌåÆ capsfilter ŌåÆ webrtcbin sink pad
- MediaStreamTrack GStreamer integration: _gstSource, _gstPipeline, enabledŌåÆvalve.drop, stop()ŌåÆNULL+dispose
- RTCRtpSender._wirePipeline builds explicit encoder chains (no Vala bridge needed ŌĆö all main-thread)
- RTCRtpSender.replaceTrack with atomic source swap (unlink old, link new, sync state)
- Capsfilter with RTP caps ensures createOffer generates m= lines immediately
- End-to-end: pcA.addTrack(getUserMedia audio) ŌåÆ pcB receives track event, track unmutes
- Single-PC-per-track limitation (multi-PC fan-out via tee deferred to future)

**Implemented (Phase 4 ŌĆö Stats & advanced):**
- RTCPeerConnection.getStats() ŌĆö emits `get-stats` signal on webrtcbin, parses `GstStructure` ŌåÆ `RTCStatsReport` (Map<string, RTCStats>) via `gst-stats-parser.ts` (snake_case ŌåÆ camelCase conversion). `getStats(track)` validates selector against live senders/receivers and rejects with `InvalidAccessError` for unknown tracks. `sender.getStats()` / `receiver.getStats()` delegate via a stats callback wired in `addTrack`/`addTransceiver`.
- RTCPeerConnection.restartIce() ŌĆö sets ICE restart flag, triggers `negotiationneeded` if negotiation is underway
- RTCPeerConnection.setConfiguration() ŌĆö validates and applies ICE server updates; rejects immutable fields (`bundlePolicy`, `rtcpMuxPolicy`) with `InvalidModificationError`
- RTCDTMFSender ŌĆö full spec-compliant tone insertion: DTMF char validation (0-9 A-D # * ,), `duration` clamping (40ŌĆō6000ms), `interToneGap` (Ōēź30ms), `toneBuffer` reader, `tonechange` event dispatch, `commaDelay` (2 s), `insertDTMF()` overwrites pending queue. Tested against `refs/wpt/webrtc/RTCDTMFSender-insertDTMF.https.html`
- RTCCertificate ŌĆö `generateCertificate(algorithm)` validates ECDSA/RSASSA-PKCS1-v1_5 params, returns certificate with 30-day expiry. `getFingerprints()`, `expires` getter. W3C API surface matches spec; actual DTLS cert is GStreamer-internal.
- RTCDtlsTransport, RTCIceTransport, RTCSctpTransport ŌĆö thin W3C proxy classes (state, iceTransport getter, maxMessageSize, maxChannels). Exposed from `@gjsify/webrtc` index.

**Still deferred (post-Phase 4):**
- `icecandidateerror` event ŌĆö stub (getter returns null, setter no-op); requires mapping webrtcbin ICE failure signals
- `peerIdentity` / `getIdentityAssertion` ŌĆö stub (rejects with TypeError); identity provider integration not planned
- `setLocalDescription()` without explicit argument ŌĆö callers must pass a `RTCSessionDescriptionInit`
- MediaStreamTrack constraints (`applyConstraints`, `getConstraints`, `getCapabilities` per-device)
- `enumerateDevices` with GStreamer Device Monitor
- Multi-PC-per-track fan-out via tee multiplexer

**Notes on spec behaviour (verified against WPT):**
- RTCDataChannel.binaryType defaults to `'arraybuffer'` ŌĆö this IS the W3C spec default (┬¦6.2: *"The initial value is 'arraybuffer'"*), distinct from WebSocket which defaults to `'blob'`. Invalid assignments are silently ignored per WPT [RTCDataChannel-binaryType.window.js](refs/wpt/webrtc/RTCDataChannel-binaryType.window.js) (matches Firefox / Chrome / Safari).
- Setting `binaryType` to `'blob'` requires `globalThis.Blob` (provide via `@gjsify/buffer/register`); otherwise the setter throws `NotSupportedError`.

**Current deviation from W3C spec:**
- `setLocalDescription()` without a description argument (implicit createOffer/createAnswer re-use) is not implemented ŌĆö callers must pass an explicit `RTCSessionDescriptionInit`.

**How the GJS streaming-thread issue is solved (Phase 1.5):**

Webrtcbin emits `on-negotiation-needed`, `on-ice-candidate`, `on-data-channel` (and its `Gst.Promise` change_func callbacks) from GStreamer's internal streaming thread. GJS/SpiderMonkey blocks any JS callback invoked from a non-main thread (critical log: *"Attempting to call back into JSAPI on a different thread. ŌĆ” it has been blocked."*) to prevent VM corruption. An in-JS `GLib.idle_add` workaround doesn't help because the callback body itself never runs.

**`@gjsify/webrtc-native`** solves this on the C side: three Vala GObject classes (`WebrtcbinBridge`, `DataChannelBridge`, `PromiseBridge`) connect to the underlying GStreamer signals and `Gst.Promise` change_func, capture their args, then use `GLib.Idle.add()` to re-emit mirror signals on the main GLib context. JS consumers (`@gjsify/webrtc`) connect to those mirror signals and always run on the main thread.

Two subtleties in the bridge design:
1. `WebrtcbinBridge.on_data_channel_cb` wraps the incoming channel in a `DataChannelBridge` *on the streaming thread* before the idle hop ŌĆö so the bridge's own signal handlers are connected before any `on-message-*` callbacks can fire on the same thread. Without this eager wrap, the first few messages from the remote peer would race the JS-side setup and get dropped.
2. The `GstWebRTCDataChannelState` C enum is **1-based** (`CONNECTING=1 ŌĆ” CLOSED=4`) but the auto-generated TypeScript declaration omits the initialiser and infers 0-based values. `RTCDataChannel` maps against the real 1-based runtime values.

Tests: **302 total across 4 spec files** (`webrtc.spec.ts` 87, `wpt.spec.ts` 96, `wpt-media.spec.ts` 109, `register.spec.ts` 10), including the full loopback (two local peers, offer/answer, ICE trickle, data-channel open/send/receive/echo).

**System prerequisites:**
- GStreamer Ōēź 1.20 with **gst-plugins-bad** (for webrtcbin) AND **libnice-gstreamer** (for ICE transport ŌĆö webrtcbin's state-change to PLAYING fails without it)
- Fedora:   `dnf install gstreamer1-plugins-bad-free gstreamer1-plugins-bad-free-extras libnice-gstreamer1`
- Ubuntu/Debian: `apt install gstreamer1.0-plugins-bad gstreamer1.0-nice`
- Verify:   `gst-inspect-1.0 webrtcbin && gst-inspect-1.0 nicesrc`

Tests that exercise `webrtcbin` (construction, close, loopback, getStats) auto-skip with a clear message if the nice plugin is missing; the remaining 18 tests (RTCSessionDescription, RTCIceCandidate parsing, register-subpath wiring) cover the platform-agnostic code paths.

The base file (Ōēł590 lines now) keeps fields, abstract `_gl`, constructor, `_init`, `getParameter`, `getExtension`, `getSupportedExtensions`, plus the foundational `_checkOwns` / `_checkValid` / `_checkWrapper` helpers. Each split module exports a typed `*Methods` interface (declaration-merged into `WebGLContextBase`) and an `install*Methods(proto)` registration function ŌĆö the base file calls `installAllContextMethods(WebGLContextBase.prototype)` after the class declaration to sidestep the circular-import trap that prototype-merge mixins otherwise hit at module-load time. `as any` reduced from 74 ŌåÆ 44 across `packages/framework/webgl/src/`; the source-side counts dropped from 2 to 0 in `webgl-context-base.ts` and from 29 to 1 (in a doc comment) in `webgl2-rendering-context.ts`. All 860 GJS tests pass; the Three.js post-processing showcase rebuilds clean. |

### Adwaita Web Framework Roadmap

Currently 9 components ported; ~40 SCSS partials remain in the reference. Planned port order (each adds a custom element + SCSS partial + AGENTS attribution):

### WebGL Known Issues

Issues discovered while porting Three.js demos. Non-fatal but should be addressed for full compatibility.

| Issue | Severity | Details | Affected Demos |
|-------|----------|---------|----------------|
| `EXT_color_buffer_float` extension missing | Medium | Three.js requests this extension for `HalfFloatType` render targets. Not implemented in extension registry. Rendering works but with fallback quality. | LDraw, Pixel Post-Processing |
| WebGL1 `setError` calls too strict for WebGL2 | Low | Base class validation (texImage2D, renderbufferStorage, etc.) uses WebGL1 format/type rules. WebGL2 allows more combinations (R8, RG8, RGBA16F, DEPTH_COMPONENT24, etc.). Non-fatal ŌĆö native GL still executes the calls. | All WebGL2 demos |
| WebGL1 framebuffer color attachment validation too strict | Low | Base `_preCheckFramebufferStatus` only accepts RGBA/UNSIGNED_BYTE or RGBA/FLOAT. WebGL2 override delegates to native driver. WebGL1 with extensions (OES_texture_half_float) still rejects valid formats. | Post-processing with WebGL1 |

Not yet implemented (but potentially relevant for GJS projects):

| API | Priority | Notes |
|-----|----------|-------|
| ~~**ECDSA sign/verify**~~ | Ō£ō Done | Implemented in Phase 19 (RFC 6979 + FIPS 186-4) |
| ~~**RSA-PSS / RSA-OAEP**~~ | Ō£ō Done | Implemented in Phase 19 (RFC 8017, MGF1) |
| **URL/URLSearchParams (global)** | Low | Exists in @gjsify/url, missing as global export |
| **Blob/File (global)** | Low | Partially native in GJS; globals package could re-export |
| **structuredClone** | Low | Natively available in SpiderMonkey 128 |
| **Performance (global)** | Low | @gjsify/perf_hooks exists; Web export missing |

| Package | Function | Status |
|---------|----------|--------|
| **@gjsify/cli** | `gjsify build` CLI (Rolldown engine) | Full |
| **rolldown-plugin-gjsify** | Platform orchestration (GJS/Node/Browser/library) | Full |
| **rolldown-plugin-deepkit** | Deepkit type reflection (`transform`, lazy) | Full |
| **rolldown-plugin-pnp** | Yarn PnP resolver + relay through polyfill meta-pkgs | Full |
| **vite-plugin-blueprint** | Compile `.blp` files via blueprint-compilerŌåÆXML (Vite/Rollup/Rolldown) | Full |
| **vite-plugin-gettext** | xgettext/msgfmt/po2json pipeline (Vite/Rollup/Rolldown) | Full |
| **resolve-npm** | Central alias registry (60+ mappings) | Full |
| **empty** | Stub module for platform exclusion | Full |
| **lightningcss-native** | Phase D-2 POC. Vala+Rust cdylib bridge to lightningcss for GJS. Two GObject methods: `Engine.transform()` (in-memory CSS string ŌåÆ CSS string) and `Engine.bundle()` (entry CSS file ŌåÆ bundled CSS, resolves `@import` chains via lightningcss's filesystem-backed `FileProvider`). Both accept browserslist queries directly. Backs `cssAsStringPlugin` under `--app gjs` (when its `hasNativeLightningcss()` probe succeeds, the plugin transparently routes through this package; otherwise falls back to the existing npm `lightningcss` path). Ships Rust `cdylib` (`libgjsify_lightningcss.so`, ~8.3 MB) + Vala bridge (`libgjsifylightningcss.so`, ~34 KB) + GIR/typelib in `prebuilds/linux-x86_64/`. POC-only: no source-map input, no css-modules, no analyze-dependencies ŌĆö those are Phase B work. | POC |
| **lightningcss-wasm** | Phase D-2 POC (WASM track companion to `lightningcss-native`). Vendors `lightningcss-wasm@1.32.0`'s NAPI-on-WASM bundle (15.8 MiB `.wasm` + the napi-wasm runtime + the asyncify async helper). Pure-JS loader instantiates the WASM via SpiderMonkey 140's synchronous `new WebAssembly.{Module,Instance}` constructors; reads bytes via `node:fs` (resolves to `@gjsify/fs` under `--app gjs`); resolves `__getrandom_v03_custom` via `globalThis.crypto.getRandomValues` (`@gjsify/webcrypto` under `--app gjs`). **No WASI shim required** ŌĆö napi-wasm is a pure-JS NAPI host. Smoke tested under stock `gjs -m`: 0.81 ms for nesting flatten + minify of a 90 B fixture. Decision matrix: **3-5├Ś slower than native** on transforms, ~960├Ś slower cold init ŌĆö kept in tree as a fallback for unsupported architectures. | POC |
| **rolldown-native** | Phase D-2 POC. Vala+Rust cdylib bridge to rolldown for GJS. Wraps `rolldown::Bundler::generate()` (async, tokio) in a per-call current-thread runtime so JS sees a sync `bundle()` call. JSON-encoded `BundlerOptions` in (camelCase, matches rolldown's serde shape), JSON-encoded BundleOutput out (`{warnings, output: (Chunk\|Asset)[]}`). Ships Rust cdylib (`libgjsify_rolldown.so`, ~13 MB) + Vala bridge + GIR/typelib in `prebuilds/linux-x86_64/`. Smoke tested under GJS 1.88: 17 ms cold for a 3-file ESM bundle with constant-inlining + tree-shake; 25-byte minified output for a single-export entry; clear UnresolvedEntry diagnostics on missing inputs. POC-only: no JS plugins (Phase B), no watch/HMR, no incremental builds. **Build constraint**: depends on `refs/rolldown` submodule via cargo path-dep ŌĆö rolldown 0.1.0 on crates.io has broken transitive deps (rolldown_fs/oxc_resolver_fs trait mismatch). End consumers receive only the prebuilt `.so` + `.typelib` and never see the submodule. | POC |

## Priorities / Next Steps

### Completed

- ~~**Minimalist Browser Showcase + `IFrameBridge` navigation methods**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö New `showcases/dom/minimalist-browser/` (URL bar + Back / Forward / Reload + iframe content area + built-in srcdoc page library + postMessage round-trip status line). Cross-variant by construction: the shared `src/browser-demo.ts` (`BrowserCore` class with application-side history stack) operates on an `IFrameHandle` duck-type satisfied by both a real `<iframe>` element (browser variant) AND an `IFrameBridge.iframeElement` (GJS variant ŌĆö `IFrameBridge.iframeElement` IS an `HTMLIFrameElement`). Validates `@gjsify/iframe` is feature-complete against a non-trivial cross-platform application. Built-in page library (`page:welcome`, `page:about`, `page:postmessage`, `page:adwaita`) ŌĆö each carries an inline `<script>` that calls `window.parent.postMessage({type:'page-loaded', title, url}, '*')` on `DOMContentLoaded`; the parent listens via `iframe.contentWindow.addEventListener('message', ŌĆ”)` and surfaces the announcement in a status line. **`IFrameBridge` enhancement (same PR)**: added `goBack()` / `goForward()` / `canGoBack` / `canGoForward` thin wrappers around WebKit.WebView's internal back/forward navigation list. `reload()` is inherited verbatim from `WebKit.WebView` (camelCase already, no rewrap needed). The wrappers exist for apps that want to expose the WebKit-internal history list directly; both variants of this showcase use an application-side history stack instead, for parity with the browser variant where cross-origin iframes cannot be navigated via `contentWindow.history`. Showcase count: 7 ŌåÆ 8 (after rebase against #216 + #214 merge). `packages/infra/cli/showcases.json` gained the new entry; CLI rebuild lists it under DOM. Builds clean on both targets (browser bundle: 9 KiB; GJS bundle: 217 KiB).

- ~~**WebRTC Loopback Showcase promoted from `examples/dom/` to `showcases/dom/`**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö `examples/dom/webrtc-loopback/` was a private dev/test example since the early WebRTC sprint. With Phases 2-4 of `@gjsify/webrtc` complete (Media, DataChannel, Stats), the demo is now polish-ready. `git mv examples/dom/webrtc-loopback ŌåÆ showcases/dom/webrtc-loopback`; package gained a `files: ["dist"]` array, dropped `private: true` (now publishable), gained an `exports` map (`./browser`, `./loopback-demo`, `./package.json`) for website-embedding, moved `@gjsify/webrtc` from `devDependencies` to `dependencies` (runtime prebuild dep per AGENTS.md). Browser entry refactored from inline-DOM-and-go to `mount(container: HTMLElement, options?): ShowcaseHandle` returning `{pause, resume, isPaused, restart}` ŌĆö same pattern as `three-postprocessing-pixel`. New `src/browser/browser-main.ts` is the standalone entry (`mount(document.body)`); the website slideshow can call `mount()` directly without a standalone page. `packages/infra/cli/showcases.json` gained the new entry (`category: "dom"`, `needsWebgl: false`). Showcase count: 7 ŌåÆ 8. Out of scope: `webrtc-{video,dtmf,states,trickle-ice}` remain private examples for now ŌĆö `webrtc-video` is the natural second-showcase candidate (getUserMedia + media pipeline) but a separate workstream.

- ~~**Cross-process MessagePort transfer via Worker subprocess IPC (#204 follow-up)**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö `Worker.postMessage(value, [port])` now actually moves a `MessagePort` across the parent Ōåö child boundary instead of silently dropping it. New `packages/node/worker_threads/src/subprocess-port-transport.ts` (~80 LoC) defines the `SubprocessPortTransport` adapter ŌĆö same pattern as `@gjsify/iframe`'s `BridgePortTransport` (PR #198), both implementing the `MessagePortTransport` interface that `@gjsify/message-channel`'s shared MessagePort honours via its `_inner._transport` hook (PR #204). Wire format: `{ __msgport: <portId>, op: 'send' | 'close', data: ... }` JSON lines on the existing worker IPC pipe (parent's `child.stdin.write` / child bootstrap's `process.stdout.write`); orthogonal to the existing `{ type: 'message' | 'terminate' | 'error' }` lines so dispatch is unambiguous. **Parent side**: `Worker.postMessage` walks transferList for MessagePort entries, severs each one's in-process partnership, allocates a fresh portId via monotonic counter (odd ids for parent, even for child ŌĆö disjoint namespaces avoid coordination), attaches a `SubprocessPortTransport` to the kept end's `_inner._transport`, and emits a `{ __gjsifyTransferredPort: true, portId }` placeholder. The parent's stdout-reader recognises `__msgport`-key lines and routes them via the per-Worker `_portRegistry: Map<portId, MessagePort>`. **Child side**: the bootstrap (`BOOTSTRAP_CODE` in `worker.ts`) materialises port placeholders into an inline EventEmitter-shaped port object (analogous to `makeSharedBuffer`) backed by a child-side `childPortRegistry`; outbound traffic writes JSON lines to stdout. Both sides clean up on `close()` and on Worker exit (no fd or port-registry leak). 4 new integration tests in `tests/integration/worker-stress/src/cross-process-port-transfer.gjs.spec.ts` (round-trip, lifecycle close-propagation, multi-message ordering, 20 spawn/transfer/terminate cycles) ŌĆö all green; GJS integration count 1035 ŌåÆ 1057. Worker_threads unit tests (275 GJS / 270 Node) and the worker-stress Node integration suite (1169) unchanged. transferList-within-transferList chains (port-in-port) and ArrayBuffer-over-wire stay out of scope (separate Open TODOs).

- ~~**Retire the misclassified "Vala/C-shim zero-copy" Open TODO (#209 follow-up correction)**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö The "Medium priority ŌĆö True zero-copy `SharedBuffer.viewBytes()` via Vala/C shim" Open TODO added by PR #212 promised an internal alternative to the upstream GJS gap, but the strategy is technically not implementable: `JS::NewExternalArrayBuffer` requires a `JSContext*` that GJS does not expose to GObject-introspected `.so` plugins. No native package in the monorepo links against `mozjs140`; even `refs/gjs/gjs/byteArray.cpp::from_gbytes_func` can only call the JSAPI because it runs inside GJS' own C++ runtime where the JSContext is on the call stack. A Vala/C-shim that tries to call SpiderMonkey directly cannot work without first patching GJS to expose the JSContext (or land the `fromGBytesShared` helper itself). This commit removes the misclassified Open TODO and expands the "Upstream GJS Patch Candidates" entry to document *why* an internal alternative is not viable. The `viewBytes`/`toBuffer` JSDoc comments in `@gjsify/sab-native` are aligned with the corrected understanding. No code change beyond JSDoc.

- ~~**Phase G.5: `gjsify upgrade` ŌĆö `yarn upgrade-interactive` / `npm-check-updates` replacement**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö New top-level CLI command that closes the last gap in the "no Node tooling needed" promise for dependency maintenance. Interactive prompt by default (TTY-only ŌĆö non-TTY exits with a hint pointing at `--latest`/`--minor`/`--patch`); accepts comma- or space-separated indices, `1-3` ranges, `a`/`all`. Non-interactive bulk-update modes: `--latest` (allows major), `--minor` (semver-minor + patch only), `--patch` (patches only). `--filter <substr>[,<substr>...]` narrows by case-insensitive substring match against package names. `--dry-run` prints the plan without writing. `-y`/`--yes` selects all candidates in interactive mode (CI-friendly). Workspace-aware: every non-registry spec (`workspace:`, `file:`, `link:`, `git:`, `git+`, `http(s):`, `npm:`, `*`, `latest`) is skipped ŌĆö only real external npm dependencies hit the registry. Range prefix preserved on write-back (`^1.2.3` ŌåÆ `^2.0.0`, `~0.4.0` ŌåÆ `~0.5.0`, bare `1.2.3` stays bare). Registry resolution: layered `.npmrc` lookup (`~/.npmrc` ŌåÆ `<cwd>/.npmrc`) via `parseNpmrc`, with `npm_config_registry` env var winning. Parallel `fetchPackument` with 8-worker concurrency cap (re-uses `@gjsify/npm-registry`). Color-coded diff table (red=major / yellow=minor / green=patch / cyan=prerelease). package.json indent is detected and preserved on write-back. New e2e suite `tests/e2e/upgrade/` (7 tests, ~3.3s): mock npm registry stood up in-process via `http.createServer()`; the test runner uses `execFile` (async) because `execFileSync` blocks the event loop and starves the in-process HTTP server. Covers `--latest --dry-run` (no write), `--latest` (write back with prefix), `--patch`/`--minor` (semver gating), `--filter`, `workspace:` ranges skipped, empty-deps graceful exit. Wired into `test:e2e` aggregator + `test:e2e:upgrade` script. Docs: new `gjsify upgrade` section in cli-reference.

- ~~**Phase G.4: `gjsify test` ŌĆö build+run+aggregate runner**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö Collapses the per-package `build:test:{gjs,node}` + `test:{gjs,node}` + `test` script boilerplate (~5 scripts ├Ś 110 packages = ~500 entries) into a single `gjsify test` invocation. The runner locates `src/test.mts` (or `gjsify.test.entry` from `package.json`), builds it for each requested runtime via in-process `BuildAction` (no subprocess shell-out ŌĆö re-uses the same config-loading + plugin pipeline as `gjsify build`), then runs each output (`runGjsBundle` for GJS, `spawn('node', ŌĆ”)` for Node) and prints a per-runtime summary like `Ō£ģ gjs (412ms)  Ō£ģ node (88ms)`. Exit code aggregates: any build or run failure ŌåÆ non-zero. Flags: `--runtime gjs|node|all` (default `all`), `--entry`, `--outdir`, `--rebuild` (force), `--no-build` (run an existing bundle without rebuilding), `--verbose`. Skip-when-fresh logic walks the entry's `src/` tree once (ignoring `node_modules`, `dist`, `lib`, dot-dirs) and compares the newest source mtime against the outfile mtime ŌĆö `--rebuild` overrides. New `ConfigDataTest` type (`entry?`, `outdir?`, `runtimes?`) under top-level `test?` in `ConfigData`. Wired into `commands/index.ts` and the top-level yargs surface in `src/index.ts`. New e2e suite `tests/e2e/test-runner/` (5 tests, ~3.7s): happy-path build+run, failing-spec non-zero exit, `--rebuild` forces rewrite, `--no-build` runs existing bundle + errors when missing, missing-entry error message. Wired into `test:e2e` aggregator + `test:e2e:test-runner` script. Docs: new `gjsify test` section in cli-reference. Per-package migration of the script boilerplate (easy6502, ts-for-gir, gjsify-internal packages) is the follow-up ŌĆö adopting `gjsify test` per consumer is non-breaking.

- ~~**Phase G.3: `gjsify build --watch` ŌĆö rolldown-watch-backed dev loop**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö New `--watch` / `-w` flag on `gjsify build`. Drives rolldown's native `watch()` API: rebuilds on every source change, prints duration per build (`built in <N>ms`), surfaces errors without aborting the watcher, and cleanly stops on SIGINT/SIGTERM (`watcher.close()`). Library mode (`--library --watch`) rejected with a clear error ŌĆö library builds emit multiple output formats and would surface watcher rebuilds for each, defeating the dev-loop semantic. Watch is npm-`rolldown`-only (the `@gjsify/rolldown-native` engine does not expose a watcher API); calling it under the GJS-bundled CLI raises a precise error pointing at `node lib/index.js build ... --watch` or `GJSIFY_BUNDLER=npm`. Implementation: `runWatch(finalOpts)` helper in `bundler-pick.ts` (~25 LoC) lazy-imports rolldown and returns the watcher; `BuildAction.buildApp` gains an `{ watch }` opts argument and calls `runWatchLoop(...)` when set, which registers a `BUNDLE_START` / `BUNDLE_END` / `END` / `ERROR` listener (calls `event.result.close()` per spec to free plugins' `closeBundle` resources), wires SIGINT/SIGTERM ŌåÆ `watcher.close()`, runs the `applyShebang` post-hook on every successful rebuild for `--app gjs` with `shebang: true`, and awaits the watcher's `close` event so the CLI keeps the process alive until interrupted. `BuildAction.start` rejects `library + watch` early. CLI surface: `--watch` flag wired in `commands/build.ts`; `CliBuildOptions.watch?: boolean`. New e2e suite `tests/e2e/build-watch/` (2 tests, ~10s): rebuild-on-change asserts second-build outfile reflects the edited source (`first` ŌåÆ `second-edit`) + SIGINT exit-clean check; `--library --watch` rejected with non-zero exit and matching error message. Wired into `test:e2e` aggregator and `test:e2e:build-watch` script. Docs: build flag matrix gained the `--watch` row.

- ~~**Phase F.10.3: `gjsify flatpak release` ŌĆö release-to-Flathub orchestrator**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö Thin imperative wrapper chaining `flatpak init --force` (regen assets from `gjsify.flatpak` config) ŌåÆ `flatpak check` (linters) ŌåÆ `git tag <version>` + `git push origin <version>` ŌåÆ `flatpak sync-flathub --version <version>` (Phase F.10.1). Critical ordering invariant: `init` + `check` MUST succeed before the tag is created, so a half-released state (tag exists but lint failed) never lands. Each sub-step shells out to the same CLI binary via `spawn('node', ['<cli-entry>', 'flatpak', '<sub>', ...])` so the user sees identical behaviour to running the steps by hand; fail-stop with the failing sub-command preserved in the error. Flags: positional `<version>`, `--skip-init` / `--skip-check` / `--skip-tag` (per-step opt-outs for partial-release recovery), `--push-tag` (default true; turn off when pushing manually later), `--flathub-repo` forwarded to sync-flathub, `--dry-run` prints the full plan without executing, `--verbose`. New 4-test e2e suite `tests/e2e/flatpak-release/` exercises `--dry-run` modes (full plan, skip combinations, `--flathub-repo` forwarding, missing-positional error). Wired into `test:e2e` aggregator + `test:e2e:flatpak-release` script. Docs: new `gjsify flatpak release` section in cli-reference.

- ~~**Phase F.10.2: `gjsify flatpak diff` ŌĆö Flathub drift detector**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö Reports version / commit drift between the local git state and the per-app Flathub tracking-repo manifest. Common failure mode it catches: a release was tagged locally, but the Flathub-repo manifest still pins the previous tag, so end-users on `flatpak install` never see the release. Resolution: `appId` from `gjsify.flatpak.appId`, `flathubRepo` from `gjsify.flatpak.flathubRepo` (default `flathub/<appId>`), local tag from `git describe --tags --abbrev=0` (or `--version <tag>`), remote tag + commit from `modules[0].sources[i]` of the Flathub manifest (fetched from `raw.githubusercontent.com/<repo>/(master|main)/<appId>.json`, fall-back across both branches). `--against <path>` reads a local file instead ŌĆö for CI / offline workflows. `--detail` prints the full Flathub source entry. Exit 0 when in sync (`Ō£ģ in sync (vX.Y.Z)`), exit 1 with `ŌØī drift detected` and an actionable hint pointing at `gjsify flatpak sync-flathub --version <local>`. New 4-test e2e suite `tests/e2e/flatpak-diff/` (offline via `--against`): in-sync match, drift detection + hint, `--detail` output, missing-file error. Wired into `test:e2e` aggregator + `test:e2e:flatpak-diff` script. Docs: new `gjsify flatpak diff` section in cli-reference.

- ~~**PnP zip-resident static reads inliner (TODO cleanup ŌĆö already solved by Rolldown migration)**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö Stale Open TODO entry traced back to PR #70 (esbuild era). The Rolldown migration ([Bundler migration: esbuild ŌåÆ Rolldown](#completed)) shipped `inlineStaticReads()` in `@gjsify/rolldown-plugin-gjsify` (`src/utils/inline-static-reads.ts`, ~540 LoC) ŌĆö runs as a `transform(code, id) order:'post'` hook independent of the PnP loader, walks every loaded `node_modules/...` source with acorn, statically evaluates `new URL(<lit>, import.meta.url)` / `fileURLToPath` / `path.{join,dirname,resolve,ŌĆ”}` compositions, reads the bytes through Node's PnP-hooked `fs` (which `@gjsify/rolldown-plugin-pnp`'s `load(id)` already proves works for zip-resident paths), and replaces the entire `readFileSync(...)` / `JSON.parse(readFileSync(...))` / `readdirSync` / `existsSync` call with a literal at build time. Handles all four patterns the original entry called out. E2E coverage: `tests/e2e/pnp-zip-static-reads/run.mjs` (2 tests covering `--app node` + `--app gjs`) ŌĆö installs a fixture package under Yarn 4 with `nodeLinker: pnp` from a packed tarball (so the source lands in `.yarn/cache/<pkg>.zip`), builds it, asserts the bundle contains the inlined literal and runs after a copy. Locally verified green (44 s). Closes the [#70](https://github.com/gjsify/gjsify/pull/70) follow-up.

- ~~**D.7c housekeeping ŌĆö clean up post-D.7d residuals**~~Ō£ō ŌĆö D.7d already completed the yarn elimination (committed `gjsify-lock.json`, swapped `.github/workflows/main.yml` + `deploy-docs.yml` to `gjs -m packages/infra/cli/dist/cli.gjs.mjs install --immutable`, migrated root `clear`/`build`/`test`/`npm:publish` scripts to `gjsify foreach`/`gjsify run`, deleted `.yarnrc.yml`/`yarn.lock`/`.yarn/releases/`).
